The **Solar System**[[d]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-19) consists of the Sun and the objects that [orbit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orbit "Orbit") it.[[11]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-IAU_Office_of_Astronomy_for_Education_y607-20) The name comes from _Sōl_, the Latin name for the [Sun](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sun "Sun").[[12]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-k349-21) It [formed about 4.6 billion years ago](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formation_and_evolution_of_the_Solar_System "Formation and evolution of the Solar System") when a dense region of a [molecular cloud](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molecular_cloud "Molecular cloud") collapsed, creating the Sun and a [protoplanetary disc](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protoplanetary_disc "Protoplanetary disc") from which the orbiting bodies assembled. The [fusion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thermonuclear_fusion "Thermonuclear fusion") of hydrogen into helium inside the Sun's [core](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stellar_core "Stellar core") releases energy, which is primarily emitted through its outer [photosphere](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Photosphere "Photosphere"). This creates a decreasing temperature [gradient](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gradient "Gradient") across the system. Over 99.86% of the Solar System's mass is located within the Sun.

The [most massive objects that orbit the Sun](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Solar_System_objects_by_size "List of Solar System objects by size") are the eight [planets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planet "Planet"). Closest to the Sun in order of increasing distance are the four [terrestrial planets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Terrestrial_planet "Terrestrial planet") – [Mercury](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mercury_(planet) "Mercury (planet)"), [Venus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus "Venus"), [Earth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earth "Earth") and [Mars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars "Mars"). Only the Earth and Mars orbit within the Sun's [habitable zone](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Habitable_zone "Habitable zone"), where liquid water can exist on the surface. Beyond the [frost line](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frost_line_(astrophysics) "Frost line (astrophysics)") at about five [astronomical units](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Astronomical_unit "Astronomical unit") (AU),[[e]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-23) are two [gas giants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gas_giant "Gas giant") – [Jupiter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jupiter "Jupiter") and [Saturn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saturn "Saturn") – and two [ice giants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ice_giant "Ice giant") – [Uranus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uranus "Uranus") and [Neptune](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neptune "Neptune"). Jupiter and Saturn possess nearly 90% of the non-stellar mass of the Solar System.

There are a vast number of less massive objects. There is a strong consensus among astronomers that the Solar System has at least nine [dwarf planets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dwarf_planet "Dwarf planet"): [Ceres](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ceres_(dwarf_planet) "Ceres (dwarf planet)"), [Orcus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orcus_(dwarf_planet) "Orcus (dwarf planet)"), [Pluto](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pluto "Pluto"), [Haumea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haumea "Haumea"), [Quaoar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quaoar "Quaoar"), [Makemake](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Makemake "Makemake"), [Gonggong](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gonggong_(dwarf_planet) "Gonggong (dwarf planet)"), [Eris](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eris_(dwarf_planet) "Eris (dwarf planet)"), and [Sedna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sedna_(dwarf_planet) "Sedna (dwarf planet)").[[f]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-24) Six planets, seven dwarf planets, and other bodies have orbiting [natural satellites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_satellite "Natural satellite"), which are commonly called 'moons', and range from [sizes of dwarf planets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planetary-mass_moon "Planetary-mass moon"), like Earth's [Moon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon "Moon"), to [moonlets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moonlet "Moonlet"). There are [small Solar System bodies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Small_Solar_System_body "Small Solar System body"), such as [asteroids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asteroid "Asteroid"), [comets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comet "Comet"), [centaurs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centaur_(minor_planet) "Centaur (minor planet)"), [meteoroids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Meteoroid "Meteoroid"), and [interplanetary dust clouds](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interplanetary_dust_cloud "Interplanetary dust cloud"). Some of these bodies are in the [asteroid belt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asteroid_belt "Asteroid belt") (between Mars's and Jupiter's orbit) and the [Kuiper belt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuiper_belt "Kuiper belt") (just outside Neptune's orbit).[[g]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-25)

Between the bodies of the Solar System is an [interplanetary medium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interplanetary_medium "Interplanetary medium") of dust and particles. The Solar System is constantly flooded by outflowing [charged particles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charged_particle "Charged particle") from the [solar wind](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_wind "Solar wind"), forming the [heliosphere](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heliosphere "Heliosphere"). At around 70–90 AU from the Sun, the solar wind is halted by the [interstellar medium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interstellar_medium "Interstellar medium"), resulting in the [heliopause](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heliopause_(astronomy) "Heliopause (astronomy)"). This is the boundary to [interstellar space](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interstellar_space "Interstellar space"). The Solar System extends beyond this boundary with its outermost region, the theorized [Oort cloud](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oort_cloud "Oort cloud"), the source for [long-period comets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Long-period_comet "Long-period comet"), extending to a radius of 2,000–200,000 AU. The Solar System currently moves through a cloud of interstellar medium called the [Local Cloud](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Local_Cloud "Local Cloud"). The [closest star](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_nearest_stars "List of nearest stars") to the Solar System, [Proxima Centauri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proxima_Centauri "Proxima Centauri"), is 4.25 [light-years](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Light-year "Light-year") (269,000 AU) away. Both are within the [Local Bubble](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Local_Bubble "Local Bubble"), a relatively small 1,000 light-years wide region of the [Milky Way](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Milky_Way "Milky Way").

Definition
----------

The Solar System includes the Sun and all objects that are bound to it by gravity and orbit it.[[14]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-x579-26)[[15]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-l783-27)[[16]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-n787-28)

The [International Astronomical Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Astronomical_Union "International Astronomical Union") describes the Solar System as all objects that are bound by the gravity of the Sun, the Sun itself, its eight planets, and the other celestial bodies which orbit it.[[11]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-IAU_Office_of_Astronomy_for_Education_y607-20)[NASA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NASA "NASA") describes the Solar System as a [planetary system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planetary_system "Planetary system"), including the Sun and all objects that orbit it.[[12]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-k349-21)

When not used as a proper noun and written without capitalization, "solar system" may refer to either the Solar System itself or any system reminiscent of the Solar System.[[14]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-x579-26)

Formation and evolution
-----------------------

### Past

[![Image 2](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Soot-line1.jpg/500px-Soot-line1.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Soot-line1.jpg)

Diagram of the early Solar System's [protoplanetary disk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protoplanetary_disk "Protoplanetary disk"), out of which Earth and other Solar System bodies formed

The Solar System formed at least 4.568 billion years ago from the gravitational collapse of a region within a large [molecular cloud](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molecular_cloud "Molecular cloud").[[b]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-AgeSolarSystem-2) This initial cloud was likely several light-years across and probably birthed several stars.[[18]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Arizona-30) As is typical of molecular clouds, this one consisted mostly of hydrogen, with some helium, and small amounts of heavier elements [fused](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_fusion "Nuclear fusion") by previous generations of stars.[[19]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-:3-31)

As the [pre-solar nebula](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Presolar_nebula "Presolar nebula")[[19]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-:3-31) collapsed, [conservation of angular momentum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conservation_of_angular_momentum "Conservation of angular momentum") caused it to rotate faster. The center, where most of the mass collected, became increasingly hotter than the surroundings.[[18]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Arizona-30) As the contracting nebula spun faster, it began to flatten into a [protoplanetary disc](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protoplanetary_disc "Protoplanetary disc") with a diameter of roughly 200 AU[[18]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Arizona-30)[[20]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-32) and a hot, dense [protostar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protostar "Protostar") at the center.[[21]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-33)[[22]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-34) The planets formed by [accretion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Accretion_(astrophysics) "Accretion (astrophysics)") from this disc,[[23]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-35) in which dust and gas gravitationally attracted each other, coalescing to form ever larger bodies. Hundreds of protoplanets may have existed in the early Solar System, but they either merged or were destroyed or ejected, leaving the planets, dwarf planets, and leftover [minor bodies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Small_Solar_System_body "Small Solar System body").[[24]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-bennett_8.2-36)[[25]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-37)

Due to their higher boiling points, only metals and silicates could exist in solid form in the warm inner Solar System close to the Sun (within the [frost line](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frost_line_(astrophysics) "Frost line (astrophysics)")). They eventually formed the rocky planets of Mercury, Venus, Earth, and Mars. Because these [refractory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Refractory_(planetary_science) "Refractory (planetary science)") materials only comprised a small fraction of the solar nebula, the terrestrial planets could not grow very large.[[24]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-bennett_8.2-36)

The giant planets (Jupiter, Saturn, Uranus, and Neptune) formed further out, beyond the frost line, the point between the orbits of Mars and Jupiter where material is cool enough for [volatile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volatile_(astrogeology) "Volatile (astrogeology)") icy compounds to remain solid. The ices that formed these planets were more plentiful than the metals and silicates that formed the terrestrial inner planets, allowing them to grow massive enough to capture large atmospheres of hydrogen and helium, the lightest and most abundant elements.[[24]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-bennett_8.2-36) Leftover debris that never became planets congregated in regions such as the asteroid belt, Kuiper belt, and Oort cloud.[[24]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-bennett_8.2-36)

Within 50 million years, the pressure and density of hydrogen in the center of the protostar became great enough for it to begin [thermonuclear fusion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_fusion "Nuclear fusion").[[26]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Yi2001-38) As helium accumulates at its core, the Sun is growing brighter;[[27]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-:4-39) early in its main-sequence life its brightness was 70% that of what it is today.[[28]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-40) The temperature, [reaction rate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_reaction_rate "Nuclear reaction rate"), pressure, and density increased until [hydrostatic equilibrium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hydrostatic_equilibrium "Hydrostatic equilibrium") was achieved: the thermal pressure counterbalancing the force of gravity. At this point, the Sun became a [main-sequence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Main_sequence "Main sequence") star.[[29]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-41) Solar wind from the Sun created the [heliosphere](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heliosphere "Heliosphere") and swept away the remaining gas and dust from the protoplanetary disc into interstellar space.[[27]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-:4-39)

Following the dissipation of the [protoplanetary disk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protoplanetary_disk "Protoplanetary disk"), the [Nice model](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nice_model "Nice model") proposes that [gravitational encounters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravity_assist "Gravity assist") between planetesimals and the gas giants caused each to [migrate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planetary_migration "Planetary migration") into different orbits. This led to dynamical instability of the entire system, which scattered the planetesimals and ultimately placed the gas giants in their current positions. During this period, the [grand tack hypothesis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_tack_hypothesis "Grand tack hypothesis") suggests that a final inward migration of Jupiter dispersed much of the asteroid belt, leading to the [Late Heavy Bombardment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Late_Heavy_Bombardment "Late Heavy Bombardment") of the inner planets.[[30]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-42)[[31]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-43)

### Present and future

The Solar System remains in a relatively stable, slowly evolving state by following isolated, [gravitationally bound](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravitationally_bound "Gravitationally bound") orbits around the Sun.[[32]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-44) Although the Solar System has been fairly stable for billions of years, it is technically [chaotic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chaotic_system "Chaotic system"), and may [eventually be disrupted](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stability_of_the_Solar_System "Stability of the Solar System"). There is a small chance that another star will pass through the Solar System in the next few billion years. Although this could destabilize the system and eventually lead millions of years later to expulsion of planets, collisions of planets, or planets hitting the Sun, it would most likely leave the Solar System much as it is today.[[33]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-45)

[![Image 3](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Sun_red_giant.svg/250px-Sun_red_giant.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Sun_red_giant.svg)

The current Sun compared to its peak size in the red-giant phase

The Sun's main-sequence phase, from beginning to end, will last about 10 billion years for the Sun compared to around two billion years for all other subsequent phases of the Sun's pre-[remnant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stellar_remnant "Stellar remnant") life combined.[[34]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-mnras386_1-46) The Solar System will remain roughly as it is known today until the hydrogen in the core of the Sun has been entirely converted to helium, which will occur roughly 5 billion years from now. This will mark the end of the Sun's main-sequence life. At that time, the core of the Sun will contract with hydrogen fusion occurring along a shell surrounding the inert helium, and the energy output will be greater than at present. The outer layers of the Sun will expand to roughly 260 times its current diameter, and the Sun will become a [red giant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_giant "Red giant"). Because of its increased surface area, the surface of the Sun will be cooler (2,600 K (4,220°F) at its coolest) than it is on the main sequence.[[34]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-mnras386_1-46)

The expanding Sun is expected to vaporize Mercury as well as Venus, and render Earth and Mars uninhabitable (possibly destroying Earth as well).[[35]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-47)[[36]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-48) Eventually, the core will be hot enough for helium fusion; the Sun will burn helium for a fraction of the time it burned hydrogen in the core. The Sun is not massive enough to commence the fusion of heavier elements, and nuclear reactions in the core will dwindle. Its outer layers will be ejected into space, leaving behind a dense [white dwarf](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_dwarf "White dwarf"), half the original mass of the Sun but only the size of Earth.[[34]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-mnras386_1-46) The ejected outer layers may form a [planetary nebula](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planetary_nebula "Planetary nebula"), returning some of the material that formed the Sun– but now enriched with [heavier elements](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metallicity "Metallicity") like carbon– to the [interstellar medium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interstellar_medium "Interstellar medium").[[37]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-49)[[38]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-50)

General characteristics
-----------------------

[![Image 4](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Plane_of_Ecliptic.jpg/250px-Plane_of_Ecliptic.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Plane_of_Ecliptic.jpg)

A color enhanced photopgraph from the [Moon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon "Moon") of a range of components of the Solar System. The three dots at the lower left are from left to right the planets [Saturn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saturn "Saturn"), [Mars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars "Mars"), and [Mercury](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mercury_(planet) "Mercury (planet)"), and in the middle of the picture rises the [Sun's corona](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sun%27s_corona "Sun's corona") over the dark [limb](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/limb "wiktionary:limb") of the Moon, which is from the right lit by [earthshine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earthshine "Earthshine").

Astronomers sometimes divide the Solar System structure into separate regions. The [inner Solar System](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inner_Solar_System "Inner Solar System") includes Mercury, Venus, Earth, Mars, and the bodies in the [asteroid belt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asteroid_belt "Asteroid belt"). The [outer Solar System](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Outer_Solar_System "Outer Solar System") includes Jupiter, Saturn, Uranus, Neptune, and the bodies in the [Kuiper belt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuiper_belt "Kuiper belt").[[39]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-51) Since the discovery of the Kuiper belt, the outermost parts of the Solar System are considered a distinct region consisting of [the objects beyond Neptune](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trans-Neptunian_object "Trans-Neptunian object").[[40]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-52)

### Composition

The principal component of the Solar System is the Sun, a [G-type main-sequence star](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/G-type_main-sequence_star "G-type main-sequence star") that contains 99.86% of the system's known mass and dominates it gravitationally.[[41]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-53) The Sun's four largest orbiting bodies, the giant planets, account for 99% of the remaining mass, with Jupiter and Saturn together comprising more than 90%. The remaining objects of the Solar System (including the four terrestrial planets, the dwarf planets, moons, [asteroids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asteroid "Asteroid"), and comets) together comprise less than 0.002% of the Solar System's total mass.[[h]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-footnoteD-57)

The Sun is composed of roughly 98% hydrogen and helium,[[45]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-58) as are Jupiter and Saturn.[[46]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-59)[[47]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Williams-Jupiter-60) A composition gradient exists in the Solar System, created by heat and [light pressure](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Light_pressure "Light pressure") from the early Sun; those objects closer to the Sun, which are more affected by heat and light pressure, are composed of elements with high melting points. Objects farther from the Sun are composed largely of materials with lower melting points.[[48]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-61) The boundary in the Solar System beyond which those volatile substances could coalesce is known as the [frost line](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frost_line_(astrophysics) "Frost line (astrophysics)"), and it lies at roughly five times the Earth's distance from the Sun.[[5]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Mumma-12)

### Orbits

[![Image 5](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Solar_system_orrery_inner_planets.gif/250px-Solar_system_orrery_inner_planets.gif)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Solar_system_orrery_inner_planets.gif)

Animations of the Solar System's [inner planets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inner_planet "Inner planet") orbiting. Each frame represents 2 days of motion.

[![Image 6](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Solar_system_orrery_outer_planets.gif/250px-Solar_system_orrery_outer_planets.gif)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Solar_system_orrery_outer_planets.gif)

Animations of the Solar System's [outer planets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Outer_planet "Outer planet") orbiting. This animation is 100 times faster than the inner planet animation.

The planets and other large objects in orbit around the Sun lie near the [invariable plane of the Solar System](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Invariable_plane#Solar_System "Invariable plane"), as does Earth's orbit, known as the [ecliptic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecliptic "Ecliptic"), and most closely the orbit of Jupiter, with an inclination to it of 0.3219°.[[49]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-j770-62) Smaller icy objects such as comets frequently orbit at significantly greater angles to this plane.[[50]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Levison2003-63)[[51]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-64) Most of the planets in the Solar System have secondary systems of their own, being orbited by natural satellites called moons. All of the largest natural satellites are in [synchronous rotation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Synchronous_rotation "Synchronous rotation"), with one face permanently turned toward their parent. The four giant planets have planetary rings, thin discs of tiny particles that orbit them in unison.[[52]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-bennett_4.5-65)

As a result of the [formation of the Solar System](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formation_and_evolution_of_the_Solar_System "Formation and evolution of the Solar System"), planets and most other objects orbit the Sun in the same direction that the Sun is rotating. That is, counter-clockwise, as viewed from above Earth's north pole.[[53]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-66) There are exceptions, such as [Halley's Comet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Halley%27s_Comet "Halley's Comet").[[54]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-67) Most of the larger moons orbit their planets in [prograde](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Retrograde_and_prograde_motion "Retrograde and prograde motion") direction, matching the direction of planetary rotation; Neptune's moon [Triton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Triton_(moon) "Triton (moon)") is the largest to orbit in the opposite, retrograde manner.[[55]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-68) Most larger objects rotate around their own axes in the prograde direction relative to their orbit, though the rotation of Venus is retrograde.[[56]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-69)

To a good first approximation, [Kepler's laws of planetary motion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kepler%27s_laws_of_planetary_motion "Kepler's laws of planetary motion") describe the orbits of objects around the Sun.[[57]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-:0-70): 433–437  These laws stipulate that each object travels along an [ellipse](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ellipse "Ellipse") with the Sun at one [focus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Focus_(geometry) "Focus (geometry)"), which causes the body's distance from the Sun to vary over the course of its year. A body's closest approach to the Sun is called its _[perihelion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perihelion "Perihelion")_, whereas its most distant point from the Sun is called its _[aphelion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aphelion "Aphelion")_.[[58]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-:8-71): 9-6  With the exception of Mercury, the orbits of the planets are nearly circular, but many comets, asteroids, and Kuiper belt objects follow highly elliptical orbits. Kepler's laws only account for the influence of the Sun's gravity upon an orbiting body, not the gravitational pulls of different bodies upon each other. On a human time scale, these perturbations can be accounted for using [numerical models](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Numerical_model_of_the_Solar_System "Numerical model of the Solar System"),[[58]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-:8-71): 9-6  but the planetary system can change chaotically over billions of years.[[59]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-72)

The [angular momentum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Angular_momentum "Angular momentum") of the Solar System is a measure of the total amount of orbital and [rotational momentum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rotational_momentum "Rotational momentum") possessed by all its moving components.[[60]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-73) Although the Sun dominates the system by mass, it accounts for only about 2% of the angular momentum.[[61]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Marochnik1995-74)[[62]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-75) The planets, dominated by Jupiter, account for most of the rest of the angular momentum due to the combination of their mass, orbit, and distance from the Sun, with a possibly significant contribution from comets.[[61]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Marochnik1995-74)

### Distances and scales

[![Image 7](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Orbital_distances_in_the_solar_system_linear_scale.png/250px-Orbital_distances_in_the_solar_system_linear_scale.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Orbital_distances_in_the_solar_system_linear_scale.png)

Relative orbital distances in the Solar System visualized as a condensed rectangle

The radius of the Sun is 0.0047 AU (700,000 km; 400,000 mi).[[63]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-arxiv1203_4898-76) Thus, the Sun occupies 0.00001% (1 part in 10 7) of the volume of a sphere with a radius the size of Earth's orbit, whereas Earth's volume is roughly 1 millionth (10−6) that of the Sun. Jupiter, the largest planet, is 5.2 AU from the Sun and has a radius of 71,000 km (0.00047 AU; 44,000 mi), whereas the most distant planet, Neptune, is 30 AU from the Sun.[[47]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Williams-Jupiter-60)[[64]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-77)

With a few exceptions, the farther a planet or belt is from the Sun, the larger the distance between its orbit and the orbit of the next nearest object to the Sun. For example, Venus is approximately 0.33 AU farther out from the Sun than Mercury, whereas Saturn is 4.3 AU out from Jupiter, and Neptune lies 10.5 AU out from Uranus. Attempts have been made to determine a relationship between these orbital distances, like the [Titius–Bode law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Titius%E2%80%93Bode_law "Titius–Bode law")[[65]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-78) and [Johannes Kepler's model](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mysterium_Cosmographicum "Mysterium Cosmographicum") based on the [Platonic solids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Platonic_solid "Platonic solid"),[[66]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-79) but ongoing discoveries have invalidated these hypotheses.[[67]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Boss-80)

Some [Solar System models](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System_model "Solar System model") attempt to convey the relative scales involved in the Solar System in human terms. Some are small in scale (and may be mechanical– called [orreries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orrery "Orrery"))– whereas others extend across cities or regional areas.[[68]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-81) The largest such scale model, the [Sweden Solar System](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sweden_Solar_System "Sweden Solar System"), uses the 110-meter (361-foot) [Avicii Arena](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avicii_Arena "Avicii Arena") in Stockholm as its substitute Sun, and, following the scale, Jupiter is a 7.5-meter (25-foot) sphere at [Stockholm Arlanda Airport](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stockholm_Arlanda_Airport "Stockholm Arlanda Airport"), 40 km (25 mi) away, whereas the farthest current object, [Sedna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/90377_Sedna "90377 Sedna"), is a 10 cm (4 in) sphere in [Luleå](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lule%C3%A5 "Luleå"), 912 km (567 mi) away.[[69]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-82)[[70]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Sedna-83) At that scale, the distance to Proxima Centauri would be roughly 8 times further than the Moon is from Earth.

If the Sun–Neptune distance is scaled to 100 metres (330 ft), then the Sun would be about 3 cm (1.2 in) in diameter (roughly two-thirds the diameter of a golf ball), the giant planets would be all smaller than about 3 mm (0.12 in), and [Earth's diameter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earth%27s_diameter "Earth's diameter") along with that of the other terrestrial planets would be smaller than a [flea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flea "Flea") (0.3 mm or 0.012 in) at this scale.[[71]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-84)

[![Image 8](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Solar_System_distance_to_scale.svg/960px-Solar_System_distance_to_scale.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Solar_System_distance_to_scale.svg)

Comparison of the distances between planets, with the white bar showing orbital variations. The size of the planets is not to scale.

### Habitability

[![Image 9](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/PIA21424_-_The_TRAPPIST-1_Habitable_Zone.jpg/500px-PIA21424_-_The_TRAPPIST-1_Habitable_Zone.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:PIA21424_-_The_TRAPPIST-1_Habitable_Zone.jpg)

Comparison of the habitable zones of the Solar System and [TRAPPIST-1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TRAPPIST-1 "TRAPPIST-1"), an ultracool red dwarf star known to have seven terrestrial planets in stable orbits around the star.

[![Image 10](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Diagram_of_different_habitable_zone_regions_by_Chester_Harman.jpg/500px-Diagram_of_different_habitable_zone_regions_by_Chester_Harman.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Diagram_of_different_habitable_zone_regions_by_Chester_Harman.jpg)

Besides solar energy, the primary characteristic of the Solar System enabling the presence of life is the heliosphere and planetary magnetic fields (for those planets that have them). These magnetic fields partially shield the Solar System from high-energy interstellar particles called [cosmic rays](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cosmic_ray "Cosmic ray"). The density of cosmic rays in the [interstellar medium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interstellar_medium "Interstellar medium") and the strength of the Sun's magnetic field change on very long timescales, so the level of cosmic-ray penetration in the Solar System varies, though by how much is unknown.[[72]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Langner_et_al_2005-85)

The [zone of habitability](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Circumstellar_habitable_zone "Circumstellar habitable zone") of the Solar System is conventionally located in the inner Solar System, where planetary surface or atmospheric temperatures admit the possibility of [liquid water](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liquid_water "Liquid water").[[73]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-NASA-20150407-86) Habitability might be possible in [subsurface oceans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subsurface_ocean "Subsurface ocean") of various outer Solar System moons.[[74]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-87)

Compared to many extrasolar systems, the Solar System stands out in lacking planets interior to the orbit of Mercury.[[75]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Martin082015-88)[[76]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-89) The known Solar System lacks [super-Earths](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Super-Earth "Super-Earth"), planets between one and ten times as massive as the Earth,[[75]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Martin082015-88) although the hypothetical [Planet Nine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planet_Nine "Planet Nine"), if it does exist, could be a super-Earth orbiting in the edge of the Solar System.[[77]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-90)

Uncommonly, it has only small terrestrial and large gas giants; elsewhere planets of intermediate size are typical– both rocky and gas– so there is no "gap" as seen between the size of Earth and of Neptune (with a radius 3.8 times as large). As many of these super-Earths are closer to their respective stars than Mercury is to the Sun, a hypothesis has arisen that all planetary systems start with many close-in planets, and that typically a sequence of their collisions causes consolidation of mass into few larger planets, but in case of the Solar System the collisions caused their destruction and ejection.[[75]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Martin082015-88)[[78]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-91)

The orbits of Solar System planets are nearly circular. Compared to many other systems, they have smaller [orbital eccentricity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orbital_eccentricity "Orbital eccentricity").[[75]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Martin082015-88) Although there are attempts to explain it partly with a bias in the [radial-velocity detection method](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doppler_spectroscopy "Doppler spectroscopy") and partly with long interactions of a quite high number of planets, the exact causes remain undetermined.[[75]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Martin082015-88)[[79]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-92)

Sun
---

Main article: [Sun](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sun "Sun")

[![Image 11: White ball of plasma](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/The_Sun_in_white_light.jpg/250px-The_Sun_in_white_light.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:The_Sun_in_white_light.jpg)

The Sun in true white color

The Sun is the Solar System's star and by far its most massive component. Its large mass (332,900 [Earth masses](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earth_mass "Earth mass")),[[80]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-93) which comprises 99.86% of all the mass in the Solar System,[[81]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Woolfson00-94) produces temperatures and densities in its [core](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_core "Solar core") high enough to sustain nuclear fusion of hydrogen into helium.[[82]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-95) This releases an enormous amount of [energy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Energy "Energy"), mostly [radiated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radiant_energy "Radiant energy") into [space](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Outer_space "Outer space") as [electromagnetic radiation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electromagnetic_radiation "Electromagnetic radiation") peaking in [visible light](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Visible_light "Visible light").[[83]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-96)[[84]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-97)

Because the Sun fuses hydrogen at its core, it is a main-sequence star. More specifically, it is a [G2-type main-sequence star](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/G-type_main-sequence_star "G-type main-sequence star"), where the type designation refers to its [effective temperature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Effective_temperature "Effective temperature"). Hotter main-sequence stars are more luminous but shorter lived. The Sun's temperature is intermediate between that of the [hottest stars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/O-type_main-sequence_star "O-type main-sequence star") and that of the coolest stars. Stars brighter and hotter than the Sun are rare, whereas substantially dimmer and cooler stars, known as [red dwarfs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_dwarf "Red dwarf"), make up about 75% of the [fusor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fusor_(astronomy) "Fusor (astronomy)") stars in the [Milky Way](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Milky_Way "Milky Way").[[85]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-98)

The Sun is a [population I star](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Population_I_stars "Population I stars"), having formed in the [spiral arms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spiral_arm "Spiral arm") of the [Milky Way](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Milky_Way "Milky Way") galaxy. It has a higher abundance of elements heavier than hydrogen and helium ("[metals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metallicity "Metallicity")" in astronomical parlance) than the older population II stars in the [galactic bulge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galactic_bulge "Galactic bulge") and [halo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galactic_halo "Galactic halo").[[86]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-99) Elements heavier than hydrogen and helium were formed in the cores of ancient and exploding stars, so the first generation of stars had to die before the [universe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universe "Universe") could be enriched with these atoms. The oldest stars contain few metals, whereas stars born later have more. This higher metallicity is thought to have been crucial to the Sun's development of a [planetary system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planetary_system "Planetary system") because the planets formed from the accretion of "metals".[[87]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-100)

The region of space dominated by the Solar [magnetosphere](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magnetosphere "Magnetosphere") is the [heliosphere](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heliosphere "Heliosphere"), which spans much of the Solar System. Along with [light](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sunlight "Sunlight"), the Sun radiates a continuous stream of charged particles (a [plasma](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plasma_(physics) "Plasma (physics)")) called the [solar wind](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_wind "Solar wind"). This stream spreads outwards at speeds from 900,000 kilometres per hour (560,000 mph) to 2,880,000 kilometres per hour (1,790,000 mph),[[88]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-101) filling the vacuum between the bodies of the Solar System. The result is a [thin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vacuum "Vacuum"), dusty atmosphere, called the [interplanetary medium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interplanetary_medium "Interplanetary medium"), which extends to at least 100 AU.[[89]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Voyager-102)

Activity on the Sun's surface, such as [solar flares](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_flare "Solar flare") and [coronal mass ejections](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coronal_mass_ejection "Coronal mass ejection"), disturbs the heliosphere, creating [space weather](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_weather "Space weather") and causing [geomagnetic storms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geomagnetic_storm "Geomagnetic storm").[[90]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-SunFlip-103) Coronal mass ejections and similar events blow a magnetic field and huge quantities of material from the surface of the Sun. The interaction of this magnetic field and material with Earth's magnetic field funnels charged particles into Earth's upper atmosphere, where its interactions create [aurorae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aurora_(astronomy) "Aurora (astronomy)") seen near the [magnetic poles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earth%27s_magnetic_field#Magnetic_poles "Earth's magnetic field").[[91]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-104) The largest stable structure within the heliosphere is the [heliospheric current sheet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heliospheric_current_sheet "Heliospheric current sheet"), a spiral form created by the actions of the Sun's rotating magnetic field on the interplanetary medium.[[92]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-105)[[93]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-106)

Inner Solar System
------------------

The inner Solar System is the region comprising the [terrestrial planets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#Terrestrial_planets) and the [asteroids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asteroid "Asteroid").[[94]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-107) Composed mainly of [silicates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silicate "Silicate") and metals,[[95]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-108) the objects of the inner Solar System are relatively close to the Sun; the radius of this entire region is less than the distance between the orbits of Jupiter and Saturn. This region is within the [frost line](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frost_line_(astrophysics) "Frost line (astrophysics)"), which is a little less than 5 AU from the Sun.[[50]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Levison2003-63)

### Inner planets

[![Image 12: Venus and Earth about the same size, Mars is about 0.55 times as big and Mercury is about 0.4 times as big](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Terrestrial_planet_sizes_3.jpg/250px-Terrestrial_planet_sizes_3.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Terrestrial_planet_sizes_3.jpg)

The four terrestrial planets [Mercury](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mercury_(planet) "Mercury (planet)"), [Venus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus "Venus"), [Earth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earth "Earth") and [Mars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars "Mars")

The four terrestrial or inner planets have dense, rocky compositions, few or no [moons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_satellite "Natural satellite"), and no [ring systems](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planetary_ring "Planetary ring"). They are composed largely of [refractory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Refractory_(planetary_science) "Refractory (planetary science)") minerals such as [silicates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silicates "Silicates")—which form their [crusts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crust_(geology) "Crust (geology)") and [mantles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mantle_(geology) "Mantle (geology)")—and metals such as iron and nickel which form their [cores](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planetary_core "Planetary core"). Three of the four inner planets (Venus, Earth, and Mars) have [atmospheres](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atmosphere "Atmosphere") substantial enough to generate weather; all have impact craters and [tectonic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tectonics "Tectonics") surface features, such as [rift valleys](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rift_valley "Rift valley") and volcanoes.[[96]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Ryden-109)

*   [Mercury](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mercury_(planet) "Mercury (planet)") (0.31–0.59 AU from the Sun)[[D 6]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-nasa-factsheet-110) is the smallest planet in the Solar System. Its surface is grayish, with an expansive [rupes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rupes "Rupes") (cliff) system generated from [thrust faults](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thrust_fault "Thrust fault") and bright [ray systems](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ray_system "Ray system") formed by [impact event remnants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ejecta "Ejecta").[[97]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-111) The surface has widely varying temperature, with the [equatorial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Equator "Equator") regions ranging from −170°C (−270°F) at night to 420°C (790°F) during sunlight. In the past, Mercury was volcanically active, producing smooth [basaltic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basalt "Basalt") plains similar to the Moon.[[98]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Head_et_al_1981-112) It is likely that Mercury has a silicate crust and a large iron core.[[99]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-113)[[100]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Margot2012-114) Mercury has a very tenuous atmosphere, consisting of [solar-wind](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_wind "Solar wind") particles and ejected atoms.[[101]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-115) Mercury has no natural satellites.[[102]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-spaceplace.nasa.gov-116)
*   [Venus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus "Venus") (0.72–0.73 AU)[[D 6]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-nasa-factsheet-110) has a reflective, whitish atmosphere that is mainly composed of [carbon dioxide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon_dioxide "Carbon dioxide"). At the surface, the atmospheric pressure is ninety times as dense as on Earth's sea level.[[103]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-u3r1a-117) Venus has a surface temperatures over 400°C (752°F), mainly due to the amount of [greenhouse gases](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greenhouse_gas "Greenhouse gas") in the atmosphere.[[104]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-118) The planet lacks a protective magnetic field to protect against [stripping](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atmospheric_stripping "Atmospheric stripping") by the solar wind, which suggests that its atmosphere is sustained by volcanic activity.[[105]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-119) Its surface displays extensive evidence of volcanic activity with stagnant [lid tectonics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lid_tectonics "Lid tectonics").[[106]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-120) Venus has no natural satellites.[[102]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-spaceplace.nasa.gov-116)
*   [Earth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earth "Earth") (0.98–1.02 AU)[[D 6]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-nasa-factsheet-110) is the only place in the universe where [life](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Life "Life") and [surface liquid water](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Water_distribution_on_Earth "Water distribution on Earth") are known to exist.[[107]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-life-121) Earth's atmosphere contains 78% [nitrogen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nitrogen "Nitrogen") and 21% [oxygen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxygen "Oxygen"), which is the result of the presence of life.[[108]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-handbook-122)[[109]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-NYT-20131003-123) The planet has a complex [climate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate "Climate") and [weather](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weather "Weather") system, with conditions differing drastically between [climate regions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_region "Climate region").[[110]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-climate_zones-124) The solid surface of Earth is dominated by green [vegetation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vegetation "Vegetation"), [deserts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hot_deserts "Hot deserts") and white [ice sheets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ice_sheet "Ice sheet").[[111]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Carlowicz_Simmon_2019-125)[[112]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Cain_2010-126)[[113]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-National_Geographic_Society_2006-127) Earth's surface is shaped by [plate tectonics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plate_tectonics "Plate tectonics") that formed the continental masses.[[98]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Head_et_al_1981-112) Earth's planetary [magnetosphere](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magnetosphere "Magnetosphere") shields the surface from radiation, limiting [atmospheric stripping](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atmospheric_stripping "Atmospheric stripping") and maintaining life habitability.[[114]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-128)
    *   The [Moon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon "Moon") is Earth's only natural satellite.[[115]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-129) Its diameter is one-quarter the size of Earth's.[[116]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Metzger2021-130) Its surface is covered in [very fine regolith](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_soil "Lunar soil") and dominated by [impact craters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Impact_crater "Impact crater").[[117]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-131)[[118]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-132) Large dark patches on the Moon, [maria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_mare "Lunar mare"), are formed from past volcanic activity.[[119]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-133) The Moon's atmosphere is extremely thin, consisting of a [partial vacuum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Partial_vacuum "Partial vacuum") with particle densities of under 10 7 per cm−3.[[120]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-134)

*   [Mars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars "Mars") (1.38–1.67 AU)[[D 6]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-nasa-factsheet-110) has a radius about half of that of Earth.[[121]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Seidelmann2007-135) Most of the planet is red due to [iron oxide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iron(III)_oxide "Iron(III) oxide") in Martian soil,[[122]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-136) and the polar regions are covered in [white ice caps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Martian_polar_ice_caps "Martian polar ice caps") made of water and [carbon dioxide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon_dioxide "Carbon dioxide").[[123]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-137) Mars has an atmosphere composed mostly of carbon dioxide, with surface pressure 0.6% of that of Earth, which is sufficient to support some weather phenomena.[[124]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-138) During the Mars year (687 Earth days), there are large surface temperature swings on the surface between −78.5°C (−109.3°F) to 5.7°C (42.3°F). The surface is peppered with volcanoes and [rift valleys](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rift_valley "Rift valley"), and has a rich collection of [minerals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mineral "Mineral").[[125]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-139)[[126]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-ismars-140) Mars has a highly [differentiated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planetary_differentiation "Planetary differentiation") internal structure, and lost its magnetosphere 4 billion years ago.[[127]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Nimmo_2005-141)[[128]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-swind-142)[Mars has two tiny moons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moons_of_Mars "Moons of Mars"):[[129]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-NYT-20200725-143)
    *   [Phobos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phobos_(moon) "Phobos (moon)") is Mars's inner moon. It is a small, irregularly shaped object with a mean radius of 11 km (7 mi). Its surface is very unreflective and dominated by impact craters.[[D 7]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-jplssd-144)[[130]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-145) In particular, Phobos's surface has a very large [Stickney impact crater](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stickney_(crater) "Stickney (crater)") that is roughly 4.5 km (2.8 mi) in radius.[[131]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-146)
    *   [Deimos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deimos_(moon) "Deimos (moon)") is Mars's outer moon. Like Phobos, it is irregularly shaped, with a mean radius of 6 km (4 mi) and its surface reflects little light.[[D 8]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Horizons-Deimos-147)[[D 9]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-JPLSSD-148) However, the surface of Deimos is noticeably smoother than Phobos because the regolith partially covers the impact craters.[[132]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-149)

### Asteroids

[![Image 13: Asteroid populations depicted: near-Earth asteroids, Earth trojans, Mars trojans, main asteroid belt, Jupiter trojans, Jupiter Greeks, Jupiter Hilda's triangle](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Inner_solar_system_objects_top_view_for_wiki.png/250px-Inner_solar_system_objects_top_view_for_wiki.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Inner_solar_system_objects_top_view_for_wiki.png)

Overview of the inner Solar System up to Jupiter's orbit

Asteroids, except for the largest, Ceres, are classified as [small Solar System bodies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Small_Solar_System_bodies "Small Solar System bodies") and are composed mainly of [carbonaceous](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon "Carbon"), refractory rocky and metallic minerals, with some ice.[[133]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-150)[[134]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-151) They range from a few meters to hundreds of kilometers in size. Many asteroids are divided into [asteroid groups](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asteroid_group "Asteroid group") and [families](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asteroid_family "Asteroid family") based on their orbital characteristics. Some [asteroids have natural satellites that orbit them](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minor-planet_moon "Minor-planet moon"), that is, asteroids that orbit larger asteroids.[[135]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-152)

*   [Mercury-crossing asteroids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Mercury-crossing_minor_planets "List of Mercury-crossing minor planets") are those with [perihelia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perihelia "Perihelia") within the orbit of Mercury. At least 362 are known to date, and include the closest objects to the Sun known in the Solar System.[[136]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-JPLcrosserlist-153) No [vulcanoids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vulcanoid "Vulcanoid"), asteroids between the orbit of Mercury and the Sun, have been discovered.[[137]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-154)[[138]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Steffl2013-155) As of 2024, one asteroid has been discovered to orbit completely within Venus's orbit, [594913 ꞌAylóꞌchaxnim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/594913_%EA%9E%8CAyl%C3%B3%EA%9E%8Cchaxnim "594913 ꞌAylóꞌchaxnim").[[139]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-156)
*   [Venus-crossing asteroids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus-crossing_asteroid "Venus-crossing asteroid") are those that cross the orbit of Venus. There are 2,809 as of 2015.[[140]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-jpello-157)
*   [Near-Earth asteroids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Near-Earth_object "Near-Earth object") have orbits that approach relatively close to Earth's orbit,[[141]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-MorbidelliAstIII-158) and some of them are [potentially hazardous objects](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Potentially_hazardous_object "Potentially hazardous object") because they might collide with Earth in the future.[[142]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-CNEOS-Basics-159)[[143]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-NEO-groups-160) There are over 37,000 known as of 2024.[[144]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-neo-jpl-stats-161) A number of solar-orbiting [meteoroids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Meteoroid "Meteoroid") were large enough to be tracked in space before striking Earth. It is now widely accepted that collisions in the past have had a significant role in shaping the geological and biological history of Earth.[[145]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-BROWN02-162)
*   [Mars-crossing asteroids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars-crossing_asteroids "Mars-crossing asteroids") are those with perhihelia above 1.3 AU which cross the orbit of Mars.[[146]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-163) As of 2024, NASA lists 26,182 confirmed Mars-crossing asteroids.[[140]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-jpello-157)

#### Asteroid belt

The [asteroid belt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asteroid_belt "Asteroid belt") occupies a torus-shaped region between 2.3 and 3.3 AU from the Sun, which lies between the orbits of Mars and Jupiter. It is thought to be remnants from the Solar System's formation that failed to coalesce because of the gravitational interference of Jupiter.[[147]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-164) The asteroid belt contains tens of thousands, possibly millions, of objects over one kilometer in diameter.[[148]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-165) Despite this, the total mass of the asteroid belt is unlikely to be more than a thousandth of that of Earth.[[44]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Krasinsky2002-56) The asteroid belt is very sparsely populated; spacecraft routinely pass through without incident.[[149]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-166)

[![Image 14](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/The_Four_Largest_Asteroids.jpg/250px-The_Four_Largest_Asteroids.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:The_Four_Largest_Asteroids.jpg)

The four largest asteroids: [Ceres](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ceres_(dwarf_planet) "Ceres (dwarf planet)"), [Vesta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/4_Vesta "4 Vesta"), [Pallas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2_Pallas "2 Pallas"), [Hygiea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/10_Hygiea "10 Hygiea"). Only Ceres and Vesta have been visited by a spacecraft and thus have a detailed picture.

Below are the descriptions of the three largest bodies in the asteroid belt. They are all considered to be relatively intact [protoplanets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protoplanet "Protoplanet"), a precursor stage before becoming a fully-formed planet (see [List of exceptional asteroids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_exceptional_asteroids "List of exceptional asteroids")):[[150]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-167)[[151]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-nasa-dawn20110329-168)

*   [Ceres](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ceres_(dwarf_planet) "Ceres (dwarf planet)") (2.55–2.98 AU) is the only dwarf planet in the asteroid belt.[[153]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-IAU-QA-170) It is the largest object in the belt, with a diameter of 940 km (580 mi).[[154]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Ermakov2017-171) Its surface contains a mixture of [carbon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon "Carbon"),[[155]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Nature_12_2018-172) frozen water and [hydrated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hydrate "Hydrate") minerals.[[156]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-EPSC2-173) There are signs of past [cryovolcanic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cryovolcano "Cryovolcano") activity, where [volatile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volatile_(astrogeology) "Volatile (astrogeology)") material such as water are erupted onto the surface, as seen in [surface bright spots](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bright_spots_on_Ceres "Bright spots on Ceres").[[157]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-174) Ceres has a very thin water vapor atmosphere, but practically speaking it is indistinguishable from a vacuum.[[158]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-175)
*   [Vesta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/4_Vesta "4 Vesta") (2.13–3.41 AU) is the second-largest object in the asteroid belt.[[159]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Astronomy_&_Astrophysics-176) Its fragments survive as the [Vesta asteroid family](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vesta_family "Vesta family")[[160]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-planetarysociety-177) and numerous [HED meteorites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HED_meteorite "HED meteorite") found on Earth.[[161]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Vestainterior-178) Vesta's surface, dominated by [basaltic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basalt "Basalt") and [metamorphic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metamorphic_rock "Metamorphic rock") material, has a denser composition than Ceres's.[[162]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Takeda1997-179) Its surface is marked by two giant craters: [Rheasilvia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rheasilvia "Rheasilvia") and [Veneneia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Veneneia_(crater) "Veneneia (crater)").[[163]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Schenk2012-180)
*   [Pallas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2_Pallas "2 Pallas") (2.15–2.57 AU) is the third-largest object in the asteroid belt.[[159]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Astronomy_&_Astrophysics-176) It has its own [Pallas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pallas_family "Pallas family")[asteroid family](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vesta_family "Vesta family").[[160]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-planetarysociety-177) Not much is known about Pallas because it has never been visited by a spacecraft,[[164]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-181) though its surface is predicted to be composed of silicates.[[165]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-AutoCB-19-182)

[Hilda asteroids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hilda_asteroid "Hilda asteroid") are in a 3:2 resonance with Jupiter; that is, they go around the Sun three times for every two Jovian orbits.[[166]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Barucci-183) They lie in three linked clusters between Jupiter and the main asteroid belt.

[Trojans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trojan_(celestial_body) "Trojan (celestial body)") are bodies located within another body's gravitationally stable [Lagrange points](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lagrangian_point "Lagrangian point"): [L 4](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lagrange_point#L4_and_L5 "Lagrange point"), 60° ahead in its orbit, or [L 5](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lagrange_point#L4_and_L5 "Lagrange point"), 60° behind in its orbit.[[167]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-spies-184) Every planet except Mercury is known to possess at least one trojan.[[168]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Connors-185)[[169]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-secondUranus-186)[[170]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-CeresVestatrojans-187) The [Jupiter trojan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jupiter_trojan "Jupiter trojan") population is roughly equal to that of the asteroid belt.[[171]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Yoshida2005-188) After Jupiter, Neptune possesses the most confirmed trojans, at 28.[[172]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-189)

Outer Solar System
------------------

The outer region of the Solar System is home to the [giant planets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Giant_planet "Giant planet") and their large moons. The [centaurs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centaur_(minor_planet) "Centaur (minor planet)") and many [short-period comets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Short-period_comet "Short-period comet") orbit in this region. Due to their greater distance from the Sun, the solid objects in the outer Solar System contain a higher proportion of volatiles such as water, ammonia, and methane, than planets of the inner Solar System because their lower temperatures allow these compounds to remain solid, without significant [sublimation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sublimation_(phase_transition) "Sublimation (phase transition)").[[24]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-bennett_8.2-36)

### Outer planets

[![Image 15: Jupiter and Saturn is about 2 times bigger than Uranus and Neptune, 10 times bigger than Venus and Earth, 20 times bigger than Mars and 25 times bigger than Mercury](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Planet_collage_to_scale_%28captioned%29.jpg/250px-Planet_collage_to_scale_%28captioned%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Planet_collage_to_scale_(captioned).jpg)

The outer planets [Jupiter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jupiter "Jupiter"), [Saturn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saturn "Saturn"), [Uranus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uranus "Uranus") and [Neptune](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neptune "Neptune"), compared to the inner planets Earth, Venus, Mars, and Mercury at the bottom right

The four outer planets, called giant planets or Jovian planets, collectively make up 99% of the mass orbiting the Sun.[[h]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-footnoteD-57) All four giant planets have multiple moons and a ring system, although only Saturn's rings are easily observed from Earth.[[96]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Ryden-109) Jupiter and Saturn are composed mainly of gases with extremely low melting points, such as hydrogen, helium, and [neon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neon "Neon"),[[173]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Podolak_Podolak_et_al._2000-190) hence their designation as [gas giants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gas_giant "Gas giant").[[174]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-191) Uranus and Neptune are [ice giants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ice_giants "Ice giants"),[[175]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-192) meaning they are largely composed of ['ice' in the astronomical sense](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volatile_(astrogeology) "Volatile (astrogeology)") (chemical compounds with melting points of up to a few hundred [kelvins](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kelvin "Kelvin")[[173]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Podolak_Podolak_et_al._2000-190) such as water, methane, ammonia, [hydrogen sulfide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hydrogen_sulfide "Hydrogen sulfide"), and [carbon dioxide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon_dioxide "Carbon dioxide").[[176]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Podolak_Weizman_et_al._1995-193)) Icy substances comprise the majority of the satellites of the giant planets and small objects that lie beyond Neptune's orbit.[[176]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Podolak_Weizman_et_al._1995-193)[[177]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-zeilik-194)

*   [Jupiter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jupiter "Jupiter") (4.95–5.46 AU)[[D 6]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-nasa-factsheet-110) is the biggest and most massive planet in the Solar System. On its surface, there are orange-brown and white cloud bands moving via the principles of [atmospheric circulation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atmospheric_circulation "Atmospheric circulation"), with giant storms swirling on the surface such as the [Great Red Spot](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Red_Spot "Great Red Spot") and [white 'ovals'](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oval_BA "Oval BA"). [Jupiter possesses a strong enough magnetosphere](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magnetosphere_of_Jupiter "Magnetosphere of Jupiter") to redirect [ionizing radiation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ionizing_radiation "Ionizing radiation") and cause [auroras](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aurora "Aurora") on its poles.[[178]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-195) As of 2025, Jupiter has [97 confirmed satellites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moons_of_Jupiter "Moons of Jupiter"), which can roughly be sorted into three groups: 
    *   The Amalthea group, consisting of [Metis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metis_(moon) "Metis (moon)"), [Adrastea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adrastea_(moon) "Adrastea (moon)"), [Amalthea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amalthea_(moon) "Amalthea (moon)"), and [Thebe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thebe_(moon) "Thebe (moon)"). They orbit substantially closer to Jupiter than other satellites.[[179]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-196) Materials from these natural satellites are the source of Jupiter's faint ring.[[180]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-197)
    *   The [Galilean moons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galilean_moons "Galilean moons"), consisting of [Ganymede](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ganymede_(moon) "Ganymede (moon)"), [Callisto](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Callisto_(moon) "Callisto (moon)"), [Io](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Io_(moon) "Io (moon)"), and [Europa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Europa_(moon) "Europa (moon)"). They are the largest moons of Jupiter and exhibit planetary properties.[[181]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-198)
    *   Irregular satellites, consisting of substantially smaller natural satellites. They have more distant orbits than the other objects.[[182]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-list-199)

*   [Saturn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saturn "Saturn") (9.08–10.12 AU)[[D 6]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-nasa-factsheet-110) has a distinctive visible [ring system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rings_of_Saturn "Rings of Saturn") orbiting around its equator composed of small ice and rock particles. Like Jupiter, it is mostly made of hydrogen and helium.[[183]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-200) At its north and south poles, Saturn has peculiar [hexagon-shaped storms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saturn%27s_hexagon "Saturn's hexagon") larger than the diameter of Earth. [Saturn has a magnetosphere](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magnetosphere_of_Saturn "Magnetosphere of Saturn") capable of producing weak auroras. As of 2025, Saturn has [274 confirmed satellites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moons_of_Saturn "Moons of Saturn"), grouped into: 
    *   Ring [moonlets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moonlet "Moonlet") and [shepherds](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shepherd_moon "Shepherd moon"), which orbit inside or close to Saturn's rings. A moonlet can only partially clear out dust in its orbit,[[184]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Sremcevic2007-201) while the ring shepherds are able to completely clear out dust, forming visible gaps in the rings.[[185]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Porco2005-202)
    *   Inner large satellites [Mimas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mimas "Mimas"), [Enceladus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enceladus "Enceladus"), [Tethys](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tethys_(moon) "Tethys (moon)"), and [Dione](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dione_(moon) "Dione (moon)"). These satellites orbit within [Saturn's E ring](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rings_of_Saturn#E_Ring "Rings of Saturn"). They are composed mostly of water ice and are believed to have differentiated internal structures.[[186]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-:2-203)
    *   Trojan moons [Calypso](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Calypso_(moon) "Calypso (moon)") and [Telesto](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Telesto_(moon) "Telesto (moon)") (trojans of Tethys), and [Helene](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Helene_(moon) "Helene (moon)") and [Polydeuces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polydeuces_(moon) "Polydeuces (moon)") (trojans of Dione). These small moons share their orbits with Tethys and Dione, leading or trailing either.[[187]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Calypso-204)[[188]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Polydeuces-205)
    *   Outer large satellites [Rhea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rhea_(moon) "Rhea (moon)"), [Titan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Titan_(moon) "Titan (moon)"), [Hyperion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hyperion_(moon) "Hyperion (moon)"), and [Iapetus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iapetus_(moon) "Iapetus (moon)").[[186]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-:2-203) Titan is the only satellite in the Solar System to have a substantial atmosphere.[[189]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Forget2017-206)
    *   Irregular satellites, consisting of substantially smaller natural satellites. They have more distant orbits than the other objects. [Phoebe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phoebe_(moon) "Phoebe (moon)") is the largest irregular satellite of Saturn.[[190]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Jewitt2007-207)

*   [Uranus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uranus "Uranus") (18.3–20.1 AU),[[D 6]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-nasa-factsheet-110) uniquely among the planets, orbits the Sun on its side with an [axial tilt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Axial_tilt "Axial tilt")>90°. This gives the planet extreme seasonal variation as each pole points alternately toward and then away from the Sun.[[191]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-208) Uranus's outer layer has a muted [cyan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyan "Cyan") color, but underneath these clouds are [many mysteries about its climate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_of_Uranus "Climate of Uranus"), such as unusually low [internal heat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internal_heat "Internal heat") and erratic cloud formation. As of 2025, Uranus has [28 confirmed satellites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moons_of_Uranus "Moons of Uranus"), divided into three groups: 
    *   Inner satellites, which orbit inside Uranus's ring system.[[192]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Esposito2002-209) They are very close to each other, which suggests that their orbits are [chaotic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chaotic_system "Chaotic system").[[193]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Duncan_Lissauer_1997-210)
    *   Large satellites, consisting of [Titania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Titania_(moon) "Titania (moon)"), [Oberon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oberon_(moon) "Oberon (moon)"), [Umbriel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Umbriel "Umbriel"), [Ariel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ariel_(moon) "Ariel (moon)"), and [Miranda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Miranda_(moon) "Miranda (moon)").[[194]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-211) Most of them have roughly equal amounts of rock and ice, except Miranda, which is made primarily of ice.[[195]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Hussmann_Sohl_et_al._2006-212)
    *   Irregular satellites, having more distant and eccentric orbits than the other objects.[[196]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Sheppardmoons2024-213)

*   [Neptune](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neptune "Neptune") (29.9–30.5 AU)[[D 6]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-nasa-factsheet-110) is the furthest planet known in the Solar System. Its outer atmosphere has a slightly muted cyan color, with occasional storms on the surface that look like dark spots. Like Uranus, many atmospheric phenomena of Neptune are unexplained, such as the [thermosphere](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thermosphere "Thermosphere")'s abnormally high temperature or the strong tilt (47°) of its magnetosphere. As of 2025, Neptune has [16 confirmed satellites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moons_of_Neptune "Moons of Neptune"), divided into two groups: 
    *   Regular satellites, which have circular orbits that lie near Neptune's equator.[[190]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Jewitt2007-207)
    *   Irregular satellites, which as the name implies, have less regular orbits. One of them, [Triton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Triton_(moon) "Triton (moon)"), is Neptune's largest moon. It is geologically active, with erupting [geysers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geyser "Geyser") of nitrogen gas, and possesses a thin, cloudy nitrogen atmosphere.[[197]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Soderblom2-214)[[189]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Forget2017-206)

### Centaurs

The centaurs are icy, comet-like bodies whose [semi-major axes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semi-major_and_semi-minor_axes "Semi-major and semi-minor axes") are longer than Jupiter's and shorter than Neptune's (between 5.5 and 30 AU).
