These are former Kuiper belt and [scattered disc objects](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scattered_disc "Scattered disc") (SDOs) that were gravitationally [perturbed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perturbation_(astronomy) "Perturbation (astronomy)") closer to the Sun by the outer planets, and are expected to become comets or be ejected out of the Solar System.[[43]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Delsanti-Beyond_The_Planets-55) While most centaurs are inactive and asteroid-like, some exhibit cometary activity, such as the first centaur discovered, [2060 Chiron](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2060_Chiron "2060 Chiron"), which has been classified as a comet (95P) because it develops a coma just as comets do when they approach the Sun.[[198]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-215) The largest known centaur, [10199 Chariklo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/10199_Chariklo "10199 Chariklo"), has a diameter of about 250 km (160 mi) and is one of the few minor planets possessing a ring system.[[199]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-spitzer-216)[[200]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Braga-Ribas-2014-217)

Trans-Neptunian region
----------------------

Beyond the orbit of Neptune lies the area of the "[trans-Neptunian region](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trans-Neptunian_object "Trans-Neptunian object")", with the doughnut-shaped Kuiper belt, home of Pluto and several other dwarf planets, and an overlapping disc of scattered objects, which is [tilted toward the plane](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orbital_inclination "Orbital inclination") of the Solar System and reaches much further out than the Kuiper belt. The entire region is still [largely unexplored](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_Solar_System_exploration "Timeline of Solar System exploration"). It appears to consist overwhelmingly of many thousands of small worlds– the largest having a diameter only a fifth that of Earth and a mass far smaller than that of the Moon– composed mainly of rock and ice. This region is sometimes described as the "third zone of the Solar System", enclosing the inner and the outer Solar System.[[201]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-218)

### Kuiper belt

[![Image 16](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Kuiper_belt_plot_objects_of_outer_solar_system.png/250px-Kuiper_belt_plot_objects_of_outer_solar_system.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Kuiper_belt_plot_objects_of_outer_solar_system.png)

Plot of objects around the [Kuiper belt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuiper_belt "Kuiper belt") and other asteroid populations. J, S, U and N denotes Jupiter, Saturn, Uranus and Neptune.

[![Image 17](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/TheKuiperBelt_classes-en.svg/250px-TheKuiperBelt_classes-en.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:TheKuiperBelt_classes-en.svg)

Orbit classification of Kuiper belt objects. Some clusters that is subjected to [orbital resonance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orbital_resonance "Orbital resonance") are marked.

The Kuiper belt is a great ring of debris similar to the asteroid belt, but consisting mainly of objects composed primarily of ice.[[202]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-physical-219) It extends between 30 and 50 AU from the Sun. It is composed mainly of small Solar System bodies, although the largest few are probably large enough to be dwarf planets.[[203]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Grundy2019-220) There are estimated to be over 100,000 Kuiper belt objects with a diameter greater than 50 km (30 mi), but the total mass of the Kuiper belt is thought to be only a tenth or even a hundredth the mass of Earth.[[43]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Delsanti-Beyond_The_Planets-55) Many Kuiper belt objects have satellites,[[204]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-221) and most have orbits that are substantially inclined (~10°) to the plane of the ecliptic.[[205]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-trojan-222)

The Kuiper belt can be roughly divided into the "[classical](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Classical_Kuiper_belt_object "Classical Kuiper belt object")" belt and the [resonant trans-Neptunian objects](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Resonant_trans-Neptunian_object "Resonant trans-Neptunian object").[[202]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-physical-219) The latter have orbits whose periods are in a simple ratio to that of Neptune: for example, going around the Sun twice for every three times that Neptune does, or once for every two. The classical belt consists of objects having no resonance with Neptune, and extends from roughly 39.4 to 47.7 AU.[[206]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-223) Members of the classical Kuiper belt are sometimes called "cubewanos", after the first of their kind to be discovered, originally designated [1992 _QB 1_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/15760_Albion "15760 Albion"), (and has since been named Albion); they are still in near primordial, low-eccentricity orbits.[[207]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-224)

There is strong consensus among astronomers that five members of the Kuiper belt are dwarf planets.[[203]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Grundy2019-220)[[208]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-JWST-225) Many dwarf planet candidates are being considered, pending further data for verification.[[209]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Tancredi2008-226)

*   [Pluto](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pluto "Pluto") (29.7–49.3 AU) is the largest known object in the Kuiper belt. Pluto has a relatively eccentric orbit, inclined 17 degrees to the [ecliptic plane](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecliptic_plane "Ecliptic plane"). Pluto has a [2:3 resonance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orbital_resonance "Orbital resonance") with Neptune, meaning that Pluto orbits twice around the Sun for every three Neptunian orbits. Kuiper belt objects whose orbits share this resonance are called [plutinos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plutino "Plutino").[[210]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Fajans_et_al_2001-227)[Pluto has five moons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moons_of_Pluto "Moons of Pluto"): Charon, [Styx](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Styx_(moon) "Styx (moon)"), [Nix](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nix_(moon) "Nix (moon)"), [Kerberos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kerberos_(moon) "Kerberos (moon)"), and [Hydra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hydra_(moon) "Hydra (moon)").[[211]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-228)
    *   [Charon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charon_(moon) "Charon (moon)"), the largest of Pluto's moons, is sometimes described as part of a [binary system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Binary_system_(astronomy) "Binary system (astronomy)") with Pluto, as the two bodies orbit a [barycenter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barycenter "Barycenter") of gravity above their surfaces (i.e. they appear to "orbit each other").

*   [Orcus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orcus_(dwarf_planet) "Orcus (dwarf planet)") (30.3–48.1 AU), is in the same 2:3 orbital resonance with Neptune as Pluto, and is the largest such object after Pluto itself.[[212]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-brownlargest-229) Its eccentricity and inclination are similar to Pluto's, but its perihelion lies about 120° from that of Pluto. Thus, the [phase](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phase_(waves)#Phase_difference "Phase (waves)") of Orcus's orbit is opposite to Pluto's: Orcus is at aphelion (most recently in 2019) around when Pluto is at perihelion (most recently in 1989) and vice versa.[[213]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-MPC2004-D15-230) For this reason, it has been called the _anti-Pluto_.[[214]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-MBP-231)[[215]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-232) It has one known moon, [Vanth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vanth_(moon) "Vanth (moon)").[[216]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-IAUC8812-233)
*   [Haumea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haumea "Haumea") (34.6–51.6 AU) was discovered in 2005.[[217]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-234) It is in a temporary 7:12 orbital resonance with Neptune.[[212]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-brownlargest-229) Haumea possesses a ring system, two known moons named [Hiʻiaka](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hi%CA%BBiaka_(moon) "Hiʻiaka (moon)") and [Namaka](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Namaka_(moon) "Namaka (moon)"), and rotates so quickly (once every 3.9 hours) that it is stretched into an [ellipsoid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ellipsoid "Ellipsoid"). It is part of a [collisional family](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collisional_family "Collisional family") of Kuiper belt objects that share similar orbits, which suggests a giant impact on Haumea ejected fragments into space billions of years ago.[[218]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Noviello2022-235)
*   [Makemake](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Makemake "Makemake") (38.1–52.8 AU), although smaller than Pluto, is the largest known object in the _classical_ Kuiper belt (that is, a Kuiper belt object not in a confirmed resonance with Neptune). Makemake is the brightest object in the Kuiper belt after Pluto. Discovered in 2005, it was officially named in 2009.[[219]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-236) Its orbit is far more inclined than Pluto's, at 29°.[[220]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Buie136472-237) It has one known moon, [S/2015 (136472) 1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/S/2015_(136472)_1 "S/2015 (136472) 1").[[221]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-ParkerA2016-238)
*   [Quaoar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quaoar "Quaoar") (41.9–45.5 AU) is the second-largest known object in the classical Kuiper belt, after Makemake. Its orbit is significantly less eccentric and inclined than those of Makemake or Haumea.[[212]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-brownlargest-229) It possesses a ring system and one known moon, [Weywot](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weywot_(moon) "Weywot (moon)").[[222]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Morgado2023-239)

### Scattered disc

[![Image 18](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/TheKuiperBelt_Projections_100AU_Classical_SDO.svg/250px-TheKuiperBelt_Projections_100AU_Classical_SDO.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:TheKuiperBelt_Projections_100AU_Classical_SDO.svg)

The orbital eccentricities and inclinations of the scattered disc population compared to the classical and resonant Kuiper belt objects

The scattered disc, which overlaps the Kuiper belt but extends out to near 500 AU, is thought to be the source of short-period comets. Scattered-disc objects are believed to have been perturbed into erratic orbits by the gravitational influence of [Neptune's early outward migration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formation_and_evolution_of_the_Solar_System#Planetary_migration "Formation and evolution of the Solar System"). Most scattered disc objects have perihelia within the Kuiper belt but aphelia far beyond it (some more than 150 AU from the Sun). SDOs' orbits can be inclined up to 46.8° from the ecliptic plane.[[223]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-240) Some astronomers consider the scattered disc to be merely another region of the Kuiper belt and describe scattered-disc objects as "scattered Kuiper belt objects".[[224]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-241) Some astronomers classify centaurs as inward-scattered Kuiper belt objects along with the outward-scattered residents of the scattered disc.[[225]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-242)

Currently, there is strong consensus among astronomers that two of the bodies in the scattered disc are dwarf planets:

*   [Eris](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eris_(dwarf_planet) "Eris (dwarf planet)") (38.3–97.5 AU) is the largest known scattered disc object and the most massive known dwarf planet. Eris's discovery contributed to a debate about the definition of a planet because it is 25% more massive than Pluto[[226]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Brown_Schaller_2007-243) and about the same diameter. It has one known moon, [Dysnomia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dysnomia_(moon) "Dysnomia (moon)"). Like Pluto, its orbit is highly eccentric, with a perihelion of 38.2 AU (roughly Pluto's distance from the Sun) and an aphelion of 97.6 AU, and steeply inclined to the ecliptic plane at an angle of 44°.[[227]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-244)
*   [Gonggong](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gonggong_(dwarf_planet) "Gonggong (dwarf planet)") (33.8–101.2 AU) is a dwarf planet in a comparable orbit to Eris, except that it is in a 3:10 resonance with Neptune.[[D 10]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-jpldata-245) It has one known moon, [Xiangliu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xiangliu_(moon) "Xiangliu (moon)").[[228]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Kissetal2017-246)

### Extreme trans-Neptunian objects

[![Image 19](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Distant_object_orbits_%2B_Planet_Nine.png/330px-Distant_object_orbits_%2B_Planet_Nine.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Distant_object_orbits_%2B_Planet_Nine.png)

The current orbits of [Sedna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/90377_Sedna "90377 Sedna"), [2012 VP113](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_VP113 "2012 VP113"), [Leleākūhonua](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/541132_Lele%C4%81k%C5%ABhonua "541132 Leleākūhonua") (pink), and other very [distant objects](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ETNO "ETNO") (red, brown and cyan) along with the predicted orbit of the hypothetical [Planet Nine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planet_Nine "Planet Nine") (dark blue)

Some objects in the Solar System have a very large orbit, and therefore are much less affected by the known giant planets than other minor planet populations. These bodies are called extreme trans-Neptunian objects, or ETNOs for short.[[229]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Sheppard-2018-247) Generally, ETNOs' [semi-major axes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semi-major_axis "Semi-major axis") are at least 150–250 AU wide.[[229]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Sheppard-2018-247)[[230]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Caju_outlier-248) For example, [541132 Leleākūhonua](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/541132_Lele%C4%81k%C5%ABhonua "541132 Leleākūhonua") orbits the Sun once every ~32,000 years, with a distance of 65–2000 AU from the Sun.[[D 11]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-jpldata2-249)

This population is divided into three subgroups by astronomers. The [scattered](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scattered_disc_object "Scattered disc object") ETNOs have [perihelia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perihelia "Perihelia") around 38–45 AU and an exceptionally high [eccentricity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orbital_eccentricity "Orbital eccentricity") of more than 0.85. As with the regular scattered disc objects, they were likely formed as result of [gravitational scattering](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planetary_migration#Gravitational_scattering "Planetary migration") by Neptune and still interact with the giant planets. The [detached](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Detached_object "Detached object") ETNOs, with perihelia approximately between 40–45 and 50–60 AU, are less affected by Neptune than the scattered ETNOs, but are still relatively close to Neptune. The [sednoids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sednoid "Sednoid") or [inner Oort cloud](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hills_Cloud "Hills Cloud") objects, with perihelia beyond 50–60 AU, are too far from Neptune to be strongly influenced by it.[[229]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Sheppard-2018-247)

Currently, there is one ETNO that is classified as a dwarf planet:

*   [Sedna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sedna_(dwarf_planet) "Sedna (dwarf planet)") (76.2–937 AU) was the first extreme trans-Neptunian object to be discovered. It is a large, reddish object, and takes ~11,400 years to complete one orbit. [Mike Brown](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_E._Brown "Michael E. Brown"), who discovered the object in 2003, asserts that it cannot be part of the scattered disc or the Kuiper belt because its perihelion is too distant to have been affected by Neptune's migration.[[231]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-250) The [sednoid population](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sednoid "Sednoid") is named after Sedna.[[229]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Sheppard-2018-247)

### Edge of the heliosphere

[![Image 20](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/PIA22835-VoyagerProgram%26Heliosphere-Chart-20181210.png/250px-PIA22835-VoyagerProgram%26Heliosphere-Chart-20181210.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:PIA22835-VoyagerProgram%26Heliosphere-Chart-20181210.png)

Diagram of the Sun's magnetosphere and helioshealth

The Sun's [stellar-wind bubble](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stellar-wind_bubble "Stellar-wind bubble"), the [heliosphere](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heliosphere "Heliosphere"), a region of space dominated by the Sun, has its boundary at the _termination shock_. Based on the Sun's [peculiar motion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peculiar_motion "Peculiar motion") relative to the [local standard of rest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Local_standard_of_rest "Local standard of rest"), this boundary is roughly 80–100 AU from the Sun upwind of the interstellar medium and roughly 200 AU from the Sun downwind.[[232]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-fahr-251) Here the solar wind collides with the interstellar medium[[233]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-252) and dramatically slows, condenses and becomes more turbulent, forming a great oval structure known as the [heliosheath](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heliosheath "Heliosheath").[[232]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-fahr-251)

The heliosheath has been theorized to look and behave very much like a comet's tail, extending outward for a further 40 AU on the upwind side but tailing many times that distance downwind to possibly several thousands of AU.[[234]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-n092-253)[[235]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-254) Evidence from the _[Cassini](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cassini\_(spacecraft) "Cassini (spacecraft)")_ and [Interstellar Boundary Explorer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interstellar_Boundary_Explorer "Interstellar Boundary Explorer") spacecraft has suggested that it is forced into a bubble shape by the constraining action of the interstellar magnetic field,[[236]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-255)[[237]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-256) but the actual shape remains unknown.[[238]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-257)

The shape and form of the outer edge of the heliosphere is likely affected by the [fluid dynamics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fluid_dynamics "Fluid dynamics") of interactions with the interstellar medium as well as [solar magnetic fields](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_magnetic_field "Solar magnetic field") prevailing to the south, e.g. it is bluntly shaped with the northern hemisphere extending 9 AU farther than the southern hemisphere.[[232]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-fahr-251) The heliopause is considered the beginning of the interstellar medium.[[89]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Voyager-102) Beyond the heliopause, at around 230 AU, lies the [bow shock](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bow_shock "Bow shock"): a plasma "wake" left by the Sun as it travels through the Milky Way.[[239]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-258) Large objects outside the heliopause remain gravitationally bound to the Sun, but the flow of matter in the interstellar medium homogenizes the distribution of micro-scale objects.[[89]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Voyager-102)

Miscellaneous populations
-------------------------

### Comets

[![Image 21: At lower left, a white coma stands out against a black background. Nebulous material streams away to the top and left, slowly fading with distance.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Comet_Hale-Bopp_1995O1.jpg/250px-Comet_Hale-Bopp_1995O1.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Comet_Hale-Bopp_1995O1.jpg)

The sparse plasma (blue) and dust (white) in the tail of [comet Hale–Bopp](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comet_Hale%E2%80%93Bopp "Comet Hale–Bopp") are being shaped by pressure from [solar radiation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sunlight "Sunlight") and the solar wind, respectively.

Comets are [small Solar System bodies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Small_Solar_System_bodies "Small Solar System bodies"), typically only a few kilometers across, composed largely of volatile ices. They have highly eccentric orbits, generally a perihelion within the orbits of the inner planets and an aphelion far beyond Pluto. When a comet enters the inner Solar System, its proximity to the Sun causes its icy surface to [sublimate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sublimation_(chemistry) "Sublimation (chemistry)") and [ionise](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ion "Ion"), creating a [coma](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coma_(cometary) "Coma (cometary)"): a long tail of gas and dust often visible to the naked eye.[[240]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-259)

Short-period comets have orbits lasting less than two hundred years. Long-period comets have orbits lasting thousands of years. Short-period comets are thought to originate in the Kuiper belt, whereas long-period comets, such as [Hale–Bopp](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comet_Hale%E2%80%93Bopp "Comet Hale–Bopp"), are thought to originate in the Oort cloud. Many comet groups, such as the [Kreutz sungrazers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kreutz_sungrazer "Kreutz sungrazer"), formed from the breakup of a single parent.[[241]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-260) Some comets with [hyperbolic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hyperbolic_trajectory "Hyperbolic trajectory") orbits may originate outside the Solar System, but determining their precise orbits is difficult.[[242]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-hyperbolic-261) Old comets whose volatiles have mostly been driven out by solar warming are often categorized as asteroids.[[243]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-262)

### Meteoroids, meteors and dust

[![Image 22](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Meteor_shower_in_the_Chilean_Desert_%28annotated_and_cropped%29.jpg/250px-Meteor_shower_in_the_Chilean_Desert_%28annotated_and_cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Meteor_shower_in_the_Chilean_Desert_(annotated_and_cropped).jpg)

The planets, zodiacal light and meteor shower (top left of image)

Solid objects smaller than one meter are usually called meteoroids and micrometeoroids (grain-sized), with the exact division between the two categories being debated over the years.[[244]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-263) By 2017, the IAU designated any solid object having a diameter between ~30[micrometers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Micrometre "Micrometre") and 1 meter as meteoroids, and depreciated the micrometeoroid categorization, instead terms smaller particles simply as 'dust particles'.[[245]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-264)

Some meteoroids formed via disintegration of comets and asteroids, while a few formed via impact debris ejected from planetary bodies. Most meteoroids are made of silicates and heavier metals like [nickel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nickel "Nickel") and [iron](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iron "Iron").[[246]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-265) When passing through the Solar System, comets produce a trail of meteoroids; it is hypothesized that this is caused either by vaporization of the comet's material or by simple breakup of dormant comets. When crossing an atmosphere, these meteoroids will produce bright streaks in the sky due to [atmospheric entry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atmospheric_entry "Atmospheric entry"), called [meteors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Meteor "Meteor"). If a stream of meteoroids enter the atmosphere on parallel trajectories, the meteors will seemingly 'radiate' from a point in the sky, hence the phenomenon's name: [meteor shower](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Meteor_shower "Meteor shower").[[247]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-266)

The inner Solar System is home to the [zodiacal dust cloud](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interplanetary_dust_cloud "Interplanetary dust cloud"), which is visible as the hazy [zodiacal light](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zodiacal_light "Zodiacal light") in dark, unpolluted skies. It may be generated by collisions within the asteroid belt brought on by gravitational interactions with the planets; a more recent proposed origin is materials from planet Mars.[[248]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-267) The outer Solar System hosts a cosmic dust cloud. It extends from about 10 AU to about 40 AU, and was probably created by collisions within the Kuiper belt.[[249]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-268)[[250]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-269)

Boundary region and uncertainties
---------------------------------

[![Image 23](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Kuiper_belt_-_Oort_cloud-en.svg/250px-Kuiper_belt_-_Oort_cloud-en.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Kuiper_belt_-_Oort_cloud-en.svg)

An [artist's impression](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artist%27s_impression "Artist's impression") of the [Oort cloud](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oort_cloud "Oort cloud"), a region still well within the [sphere of influence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sphere_of_influence_(astrodynamics) "Sphere of influence (astrodynamics)") of the Solar System, including a depiction of the much further inside [Kuiper belt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuiper_belt "Kuiper belt") (inset); the sizes of objects are over-scaled for visibility.

Much of the outer Solar System is still unknown. The region beyond 100 AU away is virtually unexplored and learning about this region of space is difficult. Study of this region depends upon inferences from those few objects whose orbits happen to be perturbed such that they fall closer to the Sun, and even then, detecting these objects has often been possible only when they happened to become bright enough to register as comets.[[251]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-270) Many objects are yet to be discovered in the Solar System's outer region.[[252]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-271)

The [Oort cloud](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oort_cloud "Oort cloud") is a theorized spherical shell of up to a trillion icy objects that is thought to be the source for all long-period comets.[[253]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-:5-272)[[254]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-:6-273) No direct observation of the Oort cloud is possible with present imaging technology.[[255]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-274) It is theorized to surround the Solar System at roughly 50,000 AU (~0.9[ly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Light-year "Light-year")) from the Sun and possibly to as far as 100,000 AU (~1.8 ly). The Oort cloud is thought to be composed of comets that were ejected from the inner Solar System by gravitational interactions with the outer planets. Oort cloud objects move very slowly, and can be perturbed by infrequent events, such as collisions, the gravitational effects of a passing star, or the [galactic tide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galactic_tide "Galactic tide"), the [tidal force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tidal_force "Tidal force") exerted by the Milky Way.[[253]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-:5-272)[[254]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-:6-273)

As of the 2020s, a few astronomers have hypothesized that [Planet Nine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planet_Nine "Planet Nine") (a planet beyond Neptune) might exist, based on statistical variance in the orbit of [extreme trans-Neptunian objects](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extreme_trans-Neptunian_object "Extreme trans-Neptunian object").[[256]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-P9H2019-275) Their closest approaches to the Sun are mostly clustered around one sector and their orbits are similarly tilted, suggesting that a large planet might be influencing their orbit over millions of years.[[257]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Sheppard2014-276)[[258]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-nodes-2021-277)[[259]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-nodes-2022-278) However, some astronomers said that this observation might be credited to observational biases or just sheer coincidence.[[260]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-279) An alternative hypothesis has a close flyby of another star disrupting the outer Solar System.[[261]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-280)

The Sun's gravitational field is estimated to [dominate the gravitational forces of surrounding stars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sphere_of_influence_(astrodynamics) "Sphere of influence (astrodynamics)") out to about two light-years (125,000 AU). Lower estimates for the radius of the Oort cloud, by contrast, do not place it farther than 50,000 AU.[[262]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Encrenaz_et_al_2004-281) Most of the mass is orbiting in the region between 3,000 and 100,000 AU.[[263]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-282) The furthest known objects, such as [Comet West](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comet_West "Comet West"), have aphelia around 70,000 AU from the Sun.[[264]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-283) The Sun's [Hill sphere](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hill_sphere "Hill sphere") with respect to the galactic nucleus, the effective range of its gravitational influence, is thought to extend up to a thousand times farther and encompasses the hypothetical Oort cloud.[[265]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Littmann-284) It was calculated by [G. A. Chebotarev](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Gleb_Alexandrovich_Chebotarev&action=edit&redlink=1 "Gleb Alexandrovich Chebotarev (page does not exist)") to be 230,000 AU.[[7]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Chebotarev-14)

[![Image 24](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Interstellar_medium_annotated.jpg/960px-Interstellar_medium_annotated.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Interstellar_medium_annotated.jpg)

The Solar System (left) within the [interstellar medium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interstellar_medium "Interstellar medium"), with the different regions and their distances on a [logarithmic scale](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logarithmic_scale "Logarithmic scale")

Celestial neighborhood
----------------------

[![Image 25](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/The_Local_Interstellar_Cloud_and_neighboring_G-cloud_complex.svg/250px-The_Local_Interstellar_Cloud_and_neighboring_G-cloud_complex.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:The_Local_Interstellar_Cloud_and_neighboring_G-cloud_complex.svg)

Diagram of the [Local Interstellar Cloud](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Local_Interstellar_Cloud "Local Interstellar Cloud"), the [G-Cloud](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/G-Cloud "G-Cloud") and surrounding stars. As of 2022, the exact position of the Solar System within the interstellar clouds remains an unresolved question in astronomy.[[266]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-285)

Within 10 light-years of the Sun there are relatively few stars, the closest being the triple star system [Alpha Centauri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alpha_Centauri "Alpha Centauri"), which is about 4.4 light-years away and may be in the Local Bubble's [G-Cloud](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/G-Cloud "G-Cloud").[[267]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-286) Alpha Centauri A and B are a closely tied pair of [Sun-like stars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_analog "Solar analog"), whereas the closest star to the Sun, the small [red dwarf](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_dwarf "Red dwarf")[Proxima Centauri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proxima_Centauri "Proxima Centauri"), orbits the pair at a distance of 0.2 light-years. In 2016, a potentially habitable [exoplanet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exoplanet "Exoplanet") was found to be orbiting Proxima Centauri, called [Proxima Centauri b](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proxima_Centauri_b "Proxima Centauri b"), the closest confirmed exoplanet to the Sun.[[268]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-proxima_b_discovery_paper-287)

The Solar System is surrounded by the [Local Interstellar Cloud](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Local_Interstellar_Cloud "Local Interstellar Cloud"), although it is not clear if it is embedded in the Local Interstellar Cloud or if it lies just outside the cloud's edge.[[269]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-:1-288) Multiple other [interstellar clouds](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interstellar_cloud "Interstellar cloud") exist in the region within 300 light-years of the Sun, known as the [Local Bubble](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Local_Bubble "Local Bubble").[[269]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-:1-288) The latter feature is an hourglass-shaped cavity or [superbubble](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Superbubble "Superbubble") in the interstellar medium roughly 300 light-years across. The bubble is suffused with high-temperature plasma, suggesting that it may be the product of several recent supernovae.[[270]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-289)

The Local Bubble is a small superbubble compared to the neighboring wider [Radcliffe Wave](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radcliffe_Wave "Radcliffe Wave") and _Split_ linear structures (formerly [Gould Belt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gould_Belt "Gould Belt")), each of which are some thousands of light-years in length.[[271]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Alves_Zucker_Goodman_Speagle_2020-290) All these structures are part of the [Orion Arm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orion_Arm "Orion Arm"), which contains most of the stars in the Milky Way that are visible to the unaided eye.[[272]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-291)

Groups of stars form together in [star clusters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Star_cluster "Star cluster"), before dissolving into co-moving associations. A prominent grouping that is visible to the naked eye is the [Ursa Major moving group](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ursa_Major_moving_group "Ursa Major moving group"), which is around 80 light-years away within the Local Bubble. The nearest star cluster is [Hyades](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hyades_(star_cluster) "Hyades (star cluster)"), which lies at the edge of the Local Bubble. The closest star-forming regions are the [Corona Australis Molecular Cloud](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Corona_Australis_Molecular_Cloud "Corona Australis Molecular Cloud"), the [Rho Ophiuchi cloud complex](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rho_Ophiuchi_cloud_complex "Rho Ophiuchi cloud complex") and the [Taurus molecular cloud](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taurus_molecular_cloud "Taurus molecular cloud"); the latter lies just beyond the Local Bubble and is part of the Radcliffe wave.[[273]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-292)

Stellar flybys that pass within 0.8 light-years of the Sun occur roughly once every 100,000 years. The [closest well-measured approach](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_nearest_stars#Distant_future_and_past_encounters "List of nearest stars") was [Scholz's Star](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scholz%27s_Star "Scholz's Star"), which approached to ~50,000 AU of the Sun some ~70 thousands years ago, likely passing through the outer Oort cloud.[[274]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-293) There is a 1% chance every billion years that a star will pass within 100 AU of the Sun, potentially disrupting the Solar System.[[275]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Raymond_et_al_2024-294)

Galactic position
-----------------

[![Image 26](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Milky_Way_side_view.png/250px-Milky_Way_side_view.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Milky_Way_side_view.png)

Diagram of the [Milky Way](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Milky_Way "Milky Way"), with galactic features and the relative position of the Solar System labeled.

The Solar System is located in the [Milky Way](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Milky_Way "Milky Way"), a [barred spiral galaxy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barred_spiral_galaxy "Barred spiral galaxy") with a diameter of about 100,000[light-years](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Light-year "Light-year") containing more than 100 billion stars.[[276]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Lang2013-295) The Sun is part of one of the Milky Way's outer spiral arms, known as the [Orion–Cygnus Arm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orion%E2%80%93Cygnus_Arm "Orion–Cygnus Arm") or Local Spur.[[277]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-296)[[278]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-297) It is a member of the [thin disk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thin_disk "Thin disk") population of stars orbiting close to the galactic plane.[[279]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-298)

Its speed around the center of the Milky Way is about 220 km/s, so that it completes one revolution every 240 million years.[[276]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Lang2013-295) This revolution is known as the Solar System's [galactic year](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galactic_year "Galactic year").[[280]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-299) The [solar apex](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_apex "Solar apex"), the direction of the Sun's path through interstellar space, is near the constellation [Hercules](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hercules_(constellation) "Hercules (constellation)") in the direction of the current location of the bright star [Vega](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vega "Vega").[[281]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-300) The plane of the ecliptic lies at an angle of about 60° to the [galactic plane](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galactic_plane "Galactic plane").[[c]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-angle-16)

The Sun follows a nearly circular orbit around the [Galactic Center](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galactic_Center "Galactic Center") (where the [supermassive black hole](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supermassive_black_hole "Supermassive black hole")[Sagittarius A*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sagittarius_A* "Sagittarius A*") resides) at a distance of 26,660 light-years,[[283]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-302) orbiting at roughly the same speed as that of the spiral arms.[[284]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-astrobiology-303) If it orbited close to the center, gravitational tugs from nearby stars could perturb bodies in the [Oort cloud](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#Oort_cloud) and send many comets into the inner Solar System, producing collisions with potentially catastrophic implications for life on Earth. In this scenario, the intense radiation of the Galactic Center could interfere with the development of complex life.[[284]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-astrobiology-303)

The Solar System's location in the Milky Way is a factor in the [evolutionary history of life](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evolutionary_history_of_life "Evolutionary history of life") on Earth. Spiral arms are home to a far larger concentration of [supernovae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supernova "Supernova"), gravitational instabilities, and radiation that could disrupt the Solar System, but since Earth stays in the Local Spur and therefore does not pass frequently through spiral arms, this has given Earth long periods of stability for life to evolve.[[284]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-astrobiology-303) However, according to the controversial [Shiva hypothesis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shiva_hypothesis "Shiva hypothesis"), the changing position of the Solar System relative to other parts of the Milky Way could explain periodic [extinction events](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extinction_events "Extinction events") on Earth.[[285]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-304)[[286]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-305)

Discovery and exploration
-------------------------

[![Image 27](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Apparent_retrograde_motion_of_Mars_in_2003.gif/250px-Apparent_retrograde_motion_of_Mars_in_2003.gif)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Apparent_retrograde_motion_of_Mars_in_2003.gif)

The motion of 'lights' moving across the sky is the basis of the classical definition of planets: wandering stars.

Humanity's knowledge of the Solar System has grown incrementally over the centuries. Up to the [Late Middle Ages](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Late_Middle_Ages "Late Middle Ages")–[Renaissance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Renaissance "Renaissance"), astronomers from Europe to India believed Earth to [be stationary at the center](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geocentrism "Geocentrism") of the universe[[287]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-306) and categorically different from the divine or ethereal objects that moved through the sky. Although the [Greek](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Greece "Ancient Greece") philosopher [Aristarchus of Samos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aristarchus_of_Samos "Aristarchus of Samos") had speculated on a [heliocentric](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heliocentric "Heliocentric") reordering of the cosmos, [Nicolaus Copernicus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nicolaus_Copernicus "Nicolaus Copernicus") was the first person known to have developed [a mathematically predictive heliocentric system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Copernican_heliocentrism "Copernican heliocentrism").[[288]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-307)[[289]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-308)

Heliocentrism did not triumph immediately over geocentrism, but the work of Copernicus had its champions, notably [Johannes Kepler](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johannes_Kepler "Johannes Kepler"). Using a heliocentric model that improved upon Copernicus by allowing orbits to be elliptical, and the precise observational data of [Tycho Brahe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tycho_Brahe "Tycho Brahe"), Kepler produced the _[Rudolphine Tables](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rudolphine\_Tables "Rudolphine Tables")_, which enabled accurate computations of the positions of the then-known planets. [Pierre Gassendi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pierre_Gassendi "Pierre Gassendi") used them to predict a [transit of Mercury](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transit_of_Mercury "Transit of Mercury") in 1631, and [Jeremiah Horrocks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeremiah_Horrocks "Jeremiah Horrocks") did the same for a [transit of Venus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transit_of_Venus "Transit of Venus") in 1639. This provided a strong vindication of heliocentrism and Kepler's elliptical orbits.[[290]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-309)[[291]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-310)

In the 17th century, [Galileo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galileo_Galilei "Galileo Galilei") publicized the use of the telescope in astronomy; he and [Simon Marius](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simon_Marius "Simon Marius") independently discovered that Jupiter had four satellites in orbit around it.[[292]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-311)[Christiaan Huygens](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christiaan_Huygens "Christiaan Huygens") followed on from these observations by discovering Saturn's moon [Titan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Titan_(moon) "Titan (moon)") and the shape of the [rings of Saturn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rings_of_Saturn "Rings of Saturn").[[293]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-312) In 1677, [Edmond Halley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edmond_Halley "Edmond Halley") observed a transit of Mercury across the Sun, leading him to realize that observations of the [solar parallax](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_parallax "Solar parallax") of a planet (more ideally using the transit of Venus) could be used to [trigonometrically](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trigonometry "Trigonometry") determine the distances between Earth, [Venus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus "Venus"), and the Sun.[[294]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-313) Halley's friend [Isaac Newton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isaac_Newton "Isaac Newton"), in his magisterial _[Principia Mathematica](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philosophi%C3%A6\_Naturalis\_Principia\_Mathematica "Philosophiæ Naturalis Principia Mathematica")_ of 1687, demonstrated that celestial bodies are not quintessentially different from Earthly ones: the same [laws of motion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Newton%27s_laws_of_motion "Newton's laws of motion") and of [gravity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Newton%27s_law_of_universal_gravitation "Newton's law of universal gravitation") apply on Earth and in the skies.[[57]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-:0-70): 142

[![Image 28](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/The_Solar_System%2C_with_the_orbits_of_5_remarkable_comets._LOC_2013593161_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-The_Solar_System%2C_with_the_orbits_of_5_remarkable_comets._LOC_2013593161_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:The_Solar_System,_with_the_orbits_of_5_remarkable_comets._LOC_2013593161_(cropped).jpg)

Solar system diagram by [Emanuel Bowen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emanuel_Bowen "Emanuel Bowen") in 1747, when neither Uranus, Neptune, nor the asteroid belts had yet been discovered. Orbits of planets are to scale, but the orbits of moons and the sizes of bodies are not.

The term "Solar System" entered the English language by 1704, when [John Locke](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Locke "John Locke") used it to refer to the Sun, planets, and comets.[[295]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-314) In 1705, Halley realized that repeated sightings of [a comet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Halley%27s_Comet "Halley's Comet") were of the same object, returning regularly once every 75–76 years. This was the first evidence that anything other than the planets repeatedly orbited the Sun,[[296]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-315) though [Seneca](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seneca_the_Younger "Seneca the Younger") had theorized this about comets in the 1st century.[[297]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-316) Careful observations of the 1769 transit of Venus allowed astronomers to calculate the average Earth–Sun distance as 93,726,900 miles (150,838,800 km), only 0.8% greater than the modern value.[[298]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-317)

[Uranus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uranus "Uranus"), having occasionally been observed since 1690 and possibly from antiquity, was recognized to be a planet orbiting beyond Saturn by 1783.[[299]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-318) In 1838, [Friedrich Bessel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Friedrich_Bessel "Friedrich Bessel") successfully measured a [stellar parallax](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stellar_parallax "Stellar parallax"), an apparent shift in the position of a star created by Earth's motion around the Sun, providing the first direct, experimental proof of heliocentrism.[[300]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-319)[Neptune](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neptune "Neptune") was identified as a planet some years later, in 1846, thanks to its gravitational pull causing a slight but detectable variation in the orbit of Uranus.[[301]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-320)[Mercury's orbital anomaly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perihelion_precession_of_Mercury "Perihelion precession of Mercury") observations led to searches for [Vulcan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vulcan_(hypothetical_planet) "Vulcan (hypothetical planet)"), a planet interior of Mercury, but these attempts were quashed with [Albert Einstein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein "Albert Einstein")'s theory of [general relativity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_relativity "General relativity") in 1915.[[302]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Clemence-321)

In the 20th century, humans began their space exploration around the Solar System, starting with placing [telescopes in space](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_telescope "Space telescope") since the 1960s.[[303]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-322) By 1989, all eight planets have been visited by space probes.[[304]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-FactSheet-323) Probes have returned samples from comets[[305]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-324) and asteroids,[[306]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-325) as well as flown through the [Sun's corona](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sun%27s_corona "Sun's corona")[[307]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-326) and visited two dwarf planets ([Pluto](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pluto "Pluto") and [Ceres](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ceres_(dwarf_planet) "Ceres (dwarf planet)")).[[308]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-327)[[309]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-NASA-20180907-328) To save on fuel, some space missions make use of [gravity assist maneuvers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravity_assist "Gravity assist"), such as the two [_Voyager_ probes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Voyager_program "Voyager program") accelerating when flying by planets in the outer Solar System[[310]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-:7-329) and the [Parker Solar Probe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parker_Solar_Probe "Parker Solar Probe") decelerating closer towards the Sun after its flyby of Venus.[[311]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-330)

Humans have landed on the Moon during the [Apollo program](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_program "Apollo program") in the 1960s and 1970s[[312]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-331) and will return to the Moon in the 2020s with the [Artemis program](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_program "Artemis program").[[313]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-sn-20230313-332) Discoveries in the 20th and 21st century has prompted the [redefinition of the term _planet_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Definition_of_planet "Definition of planet") in 2006, hence the demotion of Pluto to a dwarf planet,[[314]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-NYT-20220118-333) and further interest in [trans-Neptunian objects](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trans-Neptunian_object "Trans-Neptunian object").[[315]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-:02-334)

Notes
-----

1.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_ref-1)**The [Asteroid Belt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asteroid_Belt "Asteroid Belt"), [Kuiper Belt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuiper_Belt "Kuiper Belt"), and [Scattered Disc](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scattered_Disc "Scattered Disc") are not added because the individual asteroids are too small to be shown on the diagram.
2.   ^ [_**a**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_ref-AgeSolarSystem_2-0)[_**b**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_ref-AgeSolarSystem_2-1)The date is based on the oldest [inclusions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inclusion_(mineral) "Inclusion (mineral)") found to date in [meteorites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Meteorite "Meteorite"), 4 568.2+0.2

−0.4 million years, and is thought to be the date of the formation of the first solid material in the collapsing nebula.[[17]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-29)
3.   ^ [_**a**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_ref-angle_16-0)[_**b**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_ref-angle_16-1)If ![Image 29: {\displaystyle \psi }](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/45e5789e5d9c8f7c79744f43ecaaf8ba42a8553a) is the angle between the [north pole of the ecliptic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecliptic_pole "Ecliptic pole") and the north [galactic pole](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galactic_pole "Galactic pole") then: 

![Image 30: {\displaystyle \cos \psi =\cos(\beta _{g})\cos(\beta _{e})\cos(\alpha _{g}-\alpha _{e})+\sin(\beta _{g})\sin(\beta _{e})}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0355a973ffa402dc57f8f4371f702db85b17e989)

 where ![Image 31: {\displaystyle \beta _{g}}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/876ecaef49f096f44b57f0258336275f8ba3a373) = 27° 07′ 42.01″ and ![Image 32: {\displaystyle \alpha _{g}}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/db73983682cbebba39553ac1760903b39e050466) = 12h 51m 26.282s are the declination and right ascension of the north galactic pole,[[282]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-301) whereas ![Image 33: {\displaystyle \beta _{e}}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ea2097c0262c82b8e921dfcc2cc9873e238bc31c) = 66° 33′ 38.6″ and ![Image 34: {\displaystyle \alpha _{e}}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/5a386d5764fd35c853376fd570d4c46300b19867) = 18h 0m 00s are those for the north pole of the ecliptic. (Both pairs of coordinates are for [J2000](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J2000 "J2000") epoch.) The result of the calculation is 60.19°.
4.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_ref-19)**[Capitalization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capitalization "Capitalization") of the name varies. The [International Astronomical Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Astronomical_Union "International Astronomical Union"), the authoritative body regarding [astronomical nomenclature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Astronomical_nomenclature "Astronomical nomenclature"), specifies capitalizing the names of all individual astronomical objects but uses mixed "Solar System" and "solar system" structures in their [naming guidelines document](http://www.iau.org/public/themes/naming/)[Archived](https://web.archive.org/web/20210725053113/https://www.iau.org/public/themes/naming) 25 July 2021 at the [Wayback Machine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wayback_Machine "Wayback Machine"). The name is commonly rendered in lower case ('solar system'), as, for example, in the _[Oxford English Dictionary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxford\_English\_Dictionary "Oxford English Dictionary")_ and [_Merriam-Webster's 11th Collegiate Dictionary_](http://www.m-w.com/dictionary/solar%20system)[Archived](https://web.archive.org/web/20080127201148/http://www.m-w.com/dictionary/solar%20system) 27 January 2008 at the [Wayback Machine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wayback_Machine "Wayback Machine").
5.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_ref-23)**The scale of the Solar System is sufficiently large that astronomers use a custom unit to express distances. The [astronomical unit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Astronomical_unit "Astronomical unit"), abbreviated AU, is equal to 150,000,000 km; 93,000,000 mi. This is what the distance from the Earth to the Sun would be if the planet's orbit were perfectly circular.[[13]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-22)
6.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_ref-24)**The [International Astronomical Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Astronomical_Union "International Astronomical Union")'s Minor Planet Center has yet to officially list Orcus, Quaoar, Gonggong, and Sedna as dwarf planets as of 2024.
7.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_ref-25)**For more classifications of Solar System objects, see [List of minor-planet groups](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_minor-planet_groups "List of minor-planet groups") and [Comet §Classification](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comet#Classification "Comet").
8.   ^ [_**a**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_ref-footnoteD_57-0)[_**b**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_ref-footnoteD_57-1)The mass of the Solar System excluding the Sun, Jupiter and Saturn can be determined by adding together all the calculated masses for its largest objects and using rough calculations for the masses of the Oort cloud (estimated at roughly 3 Earth masses),[[42]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-54) the Kuiper belt (estimated at 0.1 Earth mass)[[43]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Delsanti-Beyond_The_Planets-55) and the asteroid belt (estimated to be 0.0005 Earth mass)[[44]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_note-Krasinsky2002-56) for a total, rounded upwards, of ~37 Earth masses, or 8.1% of the mass in orbit around the Sun. With the combined masses of Uranus and Neptune (~31 Earth masses) subtracted, the remaining ~6 Earth masses of material comprise 1.3% of the total orbiting mass.

101.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_ref-115)**Domingue, Deborah L.; Koehn, Patrick L.; et al. (2009). "Mercury's Atmosphere: A Surface-Bounded Exosphere". _Space Science Reviews_. **131** (1–4): 161–186. [Bibcode](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bibcode_(identifier) "Bibcode (identifier)"):[2007SSRv..131..161D](https://ui.adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2007SSRv..131..161D). [doi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doi_(identifier) "Doi (identifier)"):[10.1007/s11214-007-9260-9](https://doi.org/10.1007%2Fs11214-007-9260-9). [S2CID](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/S2CID_(identifier) "S2CID (identifier)")[121301247](https://api.semanticscholar.org/CorpusID:121301247). The composition of Mercury's exosphere, with its abundant H and He, clearly indicates a strong solar wind source. Once solar wind plasma and particles gain access to the magnetosphere, they predominantly precipitate to the surface, where solar wind species are neutralized, thermalized, and released again into the exosphere. Moreover, bombardment of the surface by solar wind particles, especially energetic ions, contributes to ejection of neutral species from the surface into the exosphere (via "sputtering") as well as other chemical and physical surface modification processes.

131.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System#cite_ref-146)**["Stickney Crater-Phobos"](http://www.solarviews.com/cap/mars/phobos2.htm). [Archived](https://web.archive.org/web/20111103010644/http://www.solarviews.com/cap/mars/phobos2.htm) from the original on 3 November 2011. Retrieved 21 April 2024. One of the most striking features of Phobos, aside from its irregular shape, is its giant crater Stickney. Because Phobos is only 28 by 20 kilometers (17 by 12 mi), it must have been nearly shattered from the force of the impact that caused the giant crater. Grooves that extend across the surface from Stickney appear to be surface fractures caused by the impact.

It thus appears smoother than Phobos because its craters lie partially buried under this loose material.
